Page 15

Free Talk

This is a Question of History 257

— Mu Mutian

Amidst the clamor of inheriting literary heritage, some people advocate "learning techniques." They say that we can't learn anything from China's past literature, and we must learn from foreign works. Our eyes should look outward.

This argument is generally correct. However, in reality, it's not a question of looking inward or outward. We should focus on the historical development of literature. Admittedly, Chinese literature is lagging behind. But this assertion holds true only when limiting the issue to a specific historical stage.

Chinese literature lags behind foreign literature only in terms of modern urban literature. Moreover, this isn't due to differences in ethnicity or nation, but mainly because China lacks modern capitalism.

If we seek profit from modern urban literature, we won't find much in China's past literary works. This is a fact. And the benefits that modern urban society's literature provides us are more numerous and undeniable. This isn't a question of China versus foreign countries, but a question of world history.

If we want to learn creative methods from modern writers, we should naturally study European and American authors like Barbusse, Gide, Gorky, Wassermann, and others, instead of blindly imitating Zhang Tianyi or other writers. Everyone knows that imitating Zhang Tianyi won't lead anywhere. This is a very clear issue in literary history, because our current society is backward.

However, the so-called literary heritage doesn't only refer to the literature of modern urban society. Homer's two great epics are heritage, and primitive ballads are also heritage. If Boileau's poems are heritage, then Du Fu's poems are certainly also heritage. The techniques of "Water Margin" aren't necessarily inferior to "Comic Novel" or "Gil Blas." Moreover, there are many pre-modern urban society and pre-Industrial Revolution Western European literary works that can provide us with literary creative methods. And, in my personal experience, Du Fu has indeed given me many benefits. The Japanese poet Kitagawa Fuyuhiko has also said that he received many instructions from Du Fu.

"Learning techniques" isn't imitating techniques. Conducting precise research on past literary works, gaining proper understanding, and thereby acquiring new techniques and new creative methods, is the issue of inheriting literary heritage. The main point is to develop old techniques. Copying-style learning may be harmful. In that case, one might narrow down the literary heritage to the smallest scope, until finally someone denies the literary heritage altogether. This contains a great danger.

The most important thing is a proper understanding of the world and life. With a correct historical understanding, any literary heritage can be inherited. New techniques can be invented from any kind of work. Baudelaire and the symbolist poets of the fin de siècle all provide us with good nourishment. The poems of Wang Wei and Du Mu are naturally the same. The main point lies in the issue of our understanding and development.

It's the establishment of creative methods or the acquisition of techniques, not copying-style learning techniques. It's a question of history, not a question of China versus foreign countries. Gaining new techniques from the study of old works is the key point. Naturally, advocating learning from Du Fu doesn't mean writing old-style poetry. Just as learning from Zola doesn't require writing in French.

Some people learn from translated works of Gorky, but due to the translations, they only learn some new vocabulary without gaining Gorky's true spirit. This isn't learning techniques, but merely slavish imitation.

What we need to pay attention to is how to inherit literary heritage. This is a question of history.

The Art of Calling 258

— Lin Xi, from Beijing

I happened to walk past Xinjiekou. I saw watermelons stacked like pyramids on the watermelon stalls. The vendors, fanning away flies with palm-leaf fans, stretched their throats and shouted, "Big juicy watermelons, have a bite!" The sound was like a magnet; whether you wanted to eat or not, you couldn't help but look at the watermelon stall. This made me think of the art of calling.

The word "bite" is very forceful. When you hear the word "bite", you're likely to think of cooling off after a ten-mile walk with a watermelon. Watermelons are so full of moisture, especially the juicy ones, that they almost drip when you bite into them. If you're not careful, the soft, crisp flesh might break off and fall. So you have to eat them quickly, biting hard and without hesitation. Afterwards, you wipe your hands and mouth, take a deep breath, and say, "Ah!" This scene is perfectly captured by the word "bite".

If I were to change "bite" to "eat", it wouldn't be so exciting. Logically, it would be too generic. It's like how saying "boat" makes people feel vague, whereas saying "fishing boat" or "steamboat" is more specific. Saying "steamboat" makes people think of waves and speed, while saying "fishing boat" makes people think of wind and sails. Just saying "boat" seems to require looking up and down. The brilliance of Wang Zhihuan's poem, "The white sun sinks behind the mountains, the Yellow River flows into the sea, to see a thousand miles further, climb another story," lies entirely in the word "story." The first three lines are no different from telling you that a thousand miles of scenery are still ahead. This half-spoken, half-swallowed way of speaking really makes you feel uncomfortable. When he says "story," that's when you can breathe a sigh of relief. This is because "story" is a level tone. Just as you are climbing, your wish is still in "to want." Only when you reach the top does it become level, comfortable, and you can see a thousand miles: see the Yellow River flowing into the sea, see distant mountains, see the white sun, see smoke, see mist, front and back. The earth is simply a big circle. That's enough flatness. With the word "story," the preceding and following text are not wasted. What if "story" were changed to "tower"? That would be terrible! Not only would the Yellow River not "flow," but it would be as if, just as you were breathing, you would have your heart broken the moment you inhaled, and you would never be able to catch your breath, just like a lifeless tower. The reason why the word "bite" is so forceful can probably be found in this line of reasoning.

This is what I thought of from "biting" watermelon. Speaking more broadly, based on the cities I've walked through, the peddlers of Beijing must be the champions of the art of calling. The purpose of calling is simply to advertise, but this kind of advertising has an immediate goal to be achieved; delaying it will lead to starvation. Therefore, being loud is the first requirement. On this point, the peddlers of Beijing undoubtedly occupy the top spot. Look at them tilting their heads and half-stroking the roots of their ears. Their voices can simply jump over the eaves and go straight into people's courtyards. In the alley where I live, there are two loud voices that resonate there every evening, one is "Fried tofu opening the pot", and the other is "Wonton opening the pot." There are also two in the morning, one is soymilk, and the other is almond tea. I'm curious, whenever they happen to be "opening the pot," they always put "opening the pot" at the end; moreover, those two words are always stretched out and vibrated so much that it really sounds like there's a pot in front of you bitterly "opening" like that. I think the beauty probably lies in the word "pot." When the word "pot" is pronounced, the lips are initially pursed so long, and then they are pulled back with a little aftertaste; therefore, it makes me think of a covered pot: opening it is so bitter and continuous, and when you lift the lid, it's like the tide receding, and the sound is louder and farther; this is exactly like retracting the lips. Therefore, the words "opening the pot" mean that the water is boiling, and at the same time they describe the scene of the pot lid being lifted; how tempting this is! The art of calling is like this.

Those who sell melons do not say the melon is bitter. Advertising always involves exaggeration, and the peddlers also know this; for example, "Big dates!" or "A big bowl for a dime!" When children hear this kind of calling, they will simply jump around their mothers. In reality, a dime is only seven or eight, far from being a big bowl. But thinking about it carefully, those three "big" characters are really shouted quite wonderfully. There are also exaggerations that are both vivid and lifelike, such as comparing radishes to pears, and persimmons to squashes. When the autumn wind brings sand and soil, big, red, and shiny persimmons can be seen everywhere in the markets of Beijing. They are certainly big enough, but compared to squashes, it's no wonder that old women would say, "How big are squashes - nonsense!" However, the persimmon vendors always shout in unison, "Squash-sized persimmons, it's okay to bite into them even if they're astringent!" These few words really describe a persimmon well enough; it's not just big, but not astringent, which is not easy to find. On winter nights, along with "hard noodles," what poets praise is the sad tune of "radish better than pears; spicy, can exchange."

Drought (Continued) 259

— Li Huiying

Yes, the work of drawing water is the most important thing right now. The fields now don't need plowing, they only need "water!"

"Ah," the son replied, proposing another idea, "Let's not go to the fields during the day tomorrow either. Let's draw water."

Having said that, he quickened his pace. The father didn't answer him, he was pondering his son's suggestion.

Arrived home.

Meals for a family of three were originally very simple, but in recent days they have been especially simple - no, it should be said they have been compressed. Compressed to the point that besides rice mixed with bran, there was only a bowl of pickled vegetable soup for each meal. Even so, Wang Axing didn't think it was enough, he even wished the family didn't eat a single grain of rice. He expected that after a prolonged drought, there would definitely be a poor harvest, and rice prices would definitely skyrocket. To prepare for the future, they should save now. However, no matter how much they save and reduce, people can't live without eating. He felt a pang of pain in his heart as he watched his son wolf down his food at the table.

It's not like his son wanted to eat more, it was simply that he needed to replenish himself after a day's labor.

"Ah Da, I think you can eat more than before."

Wang Axing's words hovered on his lips several times, before he finally said it painfully. Was it that he didn't love his son? No. But he was also afraid of a poor harvest at the end of the year, he was afraid of the unfortunate outcome, so he couldn't help but say such harsh words.

The son stared fixedly at his father's face, without replying, only calling out "Father." Although it was just one word, it contained a hidden pain that he couldn't express. The mother spoke up for her son, saying angrily:

"Aren't you going to let him eat his fill? How can he have the strength if he doesn't eat his fill! How can he work in the fields without strength? How can he draw water?"

After eating, the sun had already set behind the treetops in the west. Wang Axing didn't rest, and even forgot to smoke his usual pipe of tobacco after the meal. He urged his son to leave the house together.

Seeking 260

— Xu Yu

The dog sticks out his tongue and has no strength to bark. There is not a single sound in the bamboo forest. You can't find a single bird up or down the mountain, and you can't hear a single insect chirping to the left or right of the lake. An old man is dozing off in the field, a fishing rod for catching shrimp has slipped into the lake, the inside of the white sail is all dreams, and there are people sleeping in the thatched pavilion. I'm running wildly in this landscape because I'm looking for signs of vitality and joy, but everywhere there's tiredness and sorrow, and I'm really puzzled. So I sing foolishly by the lake, hoping for rain to break the stillness. When laughter ripples on the lake, I want to jump into that joyful lake.

I Come From the East (11) 262

— Hoshino

One hundred and fifty years ago, this "Happy Land of the Pacific" was not yet known to the world. Originally, it was a kingdom. The kingdom has been annexed into the United States for over three thousand years. Now, the bronze statue of the former monarch of Hawaii still stands tall in the harbor, worshiped by the local people. The races on the island are very complex, with yellow, white, brown, and tan skin tones, creating a mixed picture of East and West. Among the population of 360,000, Japanese people account for 140,000, almost three out of every eight Hawaiian residents are Japanese. In terms of Asians, there are also 60,000 Filipinos, 30,000 Chinese, and 3,000 Koreans. In terms of Europeans, there are 30,000 Portuguese, and about 40,000 British, American, German, and Russian people. As for pure Hawaiians, there were originally as many as 200,000, but now only 20,000 remain. The mixed race of Hawaiians and Europeans is about 15,000; the mixed race with Asians is about 12,000. Judging from the above figures, the complexity of the Hawaiian race is enough to arouse the interest of curious people.

When the ship stops at the harbor, you can smell a unique fragrance of Hawaiian plants. Local girls with yellowish-black skin, their jet-black hair scattered, swim in front of the beach with their strong and beautiful limbs. The sea is emerald green, and the sun shines on the beach, reflecting color circles like peacock tails. After seven o'clock in the evening, the slight sea breeze gently and coolly caresses the entire harbor. The best time of day in Hawaii then begins. On the mountains and hills, electric lights shine like stars in the dark night. At this time, I hired a car and drove around the island. The roads in Hawaii are very exquisitely built, and the low huts along the road are mostly shops opened by Japanese people. Many young girls, wearing cicada-wing-like thin silk clothes, stroll east, west, north, and south on the streets. Those with round faces are Japanese. Those with black arms are Hawaiians. Those wearing split cheongsams are Cantonese. Those who are tall and big with their chests out are Americans. They are all very leisurely and content. Especially the small-bodied Chinese and Japanese, as light as swallows, swimming back and forth like small crucian carp, enjoying the cool breeze of the clear night and the unique tranquil air under the coconut trees.

The beaches of Hawaii are the most famous swimming locations in the world. It's a pity that I came too late and could only walk a few steps on the beach, bringing many fine grains of white sand into my shoes. The small shops by the beach are brightly lit, and many young men and women are having a wild time drinking there. Several miles away, there is also a "Hawaiian Village," which is an open-air dance floor, with all the decorations in the original style of the natives. The village is surrounded by very tall coconut trees, with coconut oil lamps lit under the trees. Many eight or nine-year-old Hawaiian children, naked and draped in red cloth, serve as hosts. There are four or five dancing girls in the village, mostly Hawaiian. They are wearing skirts made of grass and dancing the local dance with soft limbs. The songs they sing are melodious and graceful, sometimes with a few English words inserted in the songs. Those dancing are probably guests from the ship. Americans like novelty the most, so most of the people dancing and laughing under the coconut trees are visitors who are used to seeing dancing in New York.

Lunar Eclipse 263

— Yao

According to the announcement of the Astronomical Institute of the Central Research Institute in Nanjing, there will be a "lunar eclipse" on the 26th of this month. It is found that the 26th is exactly the fifteenth day of the sixth month of the abandoned calendar, commonly known as the Mid-Month, and the people have already been preparing for the celebration ceremony on that day before the news comes.

"Lunar eclipse" is commonly known as "eating the moon," so the ancient Chinese creators of characters also knew that there would be "lunar eclipse" events in the future, and they had already planned for our grandchildren, combining "eat insect" into one word to describe this matter. The ordinary lower-class people have deeply imprinted in their minds that there will be a "black moon eating the white moon" once a year. They do not know the history of "lunar eclipse" or "no lunar eclipse," they only know that the elderly told them that this "moon eating moon" is very terrifying. If the "white moon" is eaten by the "black moon" and does not come out, the world will be destroyed immediately.... Therefore, they want to fast and celebrate, set off firecrackers, and beat gongs to scare away this "black moon." If they cannot scare it away, then it will be terrible, and the society will immediately be in chaos, and there will be no peaceful days in the world!... This unscientific understanding of theirs truly represents the semi-feudal, semi-colonial China that is indirectly ruled by the economic aggression of imperial capitalism, completely exposing the illegal organization of this current society.

On the "lunar eclipse day," the people in various places enthusiastically beat gongs and set off firecrackers, and the situation was urgent, as serious as when the news of General Shirakawa's death in the January 28th Incident spread. A sense of urgency! The air was filled in the streets of Shanghai, from about 7 pm to about 9 pm, this middle two hours was an extremely serious period. Fortunately, the people's wishes were fulfilled, and the white moon was not eaten by the black moon; otherwise, the world would not know what it would be like. At the same time, it can be said that the power of gongs and drums and firecrackers is enough to scare away the "black moon," just like "the living Buddha Zhang Tianshi set up an altar to pray for rain, and he always granted him a few times, showing their magic power..."

The entire Chinese social economy is under the serious invasion of capital imperialism today, and the wave of rural economic bankruptcy has begun to spread to cities, but under this condition, the people still have no awareness. The declining class and petty bourgeoisie who cannot get enough to eat at ordinary times feel infinite excitement on the "lunar eclipse day," just like in the amusement parks such as the Great World Tianyun Tower, they would rather suffer themselves and use the money to celebrate, anesthetizing themselves and thinking it is a meaningful night, but on the other hand, it also makes a timely business for firecracker and fast merchants, increasing their personal pockets, which is also a win-win situation.

Starting from the Students Becoming Robbers 264

— Ben

The other day, the newspaper reported that on Triumph Road in western Shanghai, a Western woman was robbed by four robbers. Later, a patrolman arrested one of the robbers, who confessed that the four who committed the robbery had always been students. This fact is not surprising in Shanghai society. I think most people who read the newspaper will just glance over it and not pay much attention to it, unlike low-level news such as adultery, which is enough to attract attention. This is also due to the special environment of Shanghai people. When glancing over it, they will not go to explore its cause and effect, which is of course also expected.

However, in the eyes of more serious people, they feel that this is not only worthy of our attention, but also worthy of our thorough understanding and research of people's minds.

China has been running new education for decades, and now, many people are shouting "education bankruptcy." The performance of this kind of student robbery is not the first time, it is truly raising the flag of this bankruptcy phenomenon, painfully imprinted in our eyes.

No matter how much education is carried out, and no matter how many schools increase year by year, it is nothing more than creating a large group of high-level vagrants. What is the reason for this? The crux is as follows: (1) Regarding education as an independent undertaking, only running education for the sake of education, without paying attention to the relationship between education and society, so creating a deformed phenomenon. (2) Regarding education as an opportunity for "personal gain," regardless of the purpose of education, regardless of the way out for education. (3) Due to the second point, most people engaged in education are running to the cities, loving to run education in the cities, and unwilling to go to the vast rural areas to run education.

In the vast rural areas, groups of basic citizens, some are very fortunate to recite a few sentences of "white-eyed text" in front of pedantic scholars, such as the Three Character Classic, but in reality, they are still blind and illiterate.

On the other hand, where are batches of middle school and university graduates going? There is no way to place them in society, they cannot be placed.

Some middle school students, whose parents have a warm heart, and they themselves hold a great hope, come out of the back door of middle school and quickly step on the front steps of university. This kind of student can be regarded as a happy child, but I don't know what percentage they account for.

However, after graduating from university, there is only a dead end to go, that is absolutely true. However, who dares and who is willing to go to a dead end? So the fact is unfolding like this:

A very small number, because they rely on the thick shade of their ancestors, turn to foreign countries to study, these are the darlings of heaven, how many can there be? Secondly, they can only go back to their hometown to eat old rice, hug the thighs of yellow-faced wives, feed their children, and play with small walnuts. I have several friends who have graduated from university who are like this. Another large group, with a rather ashamed mentality, feel that they have graduated from university but have no way out, and saying to go home to eat old rice is really better to starve to death in the city. However, can they really go to starve to death? Then they cannot, so tricks come out, and they risk trying everything dangerous.

Becoming a robber is just one of them. Please try to open your eyes and see how many sinful things in society are done by students who have always studied. The question is so serious, how to solve it, who is responsible for this?

Summer Tutoring 265

— Yi An

Respect Women 266

— Nai Ling

The Japanese writer Hakuson Kurakawa once said in his book "Impressions of Traveling in America": "When entering the dining room, the woman runs in front, and the man follows respectfully behind, this is an American couple; the woman follows the man, talking and laughing while holding hands, this is a French couple; the man sticks out his chest and belly and runs in front, and the woman follows behind him, this is an English couple." (The general idea is like this) The reason why Hakuson Kurakawa cited this example, judging from his meaning, is roughly to praise American men for "respecting women," and the men of other countries cannot keep up with them, so Hakuson Kurakawa also affirmed: "America is the golden country of women!"

Since the European wind blew into our ancient country

Page 18

, the matter of "respecting women" seems to have been noticed by us, but it is only noticed, and in terms of implementation, because of the uneven level of knowledge of the general people. Therefore, it cannot achieve universal effect; for example, we often see on the tram that women stretch out their short hands to hold the rattan ring, and men sit comfortably in their seats. Although this matter is small, it is enough to show that the general public has not yet understood what "respecting women" is all about.

Tonight, after finishing work, when I ran to the road, I saw a young couple arguing by the roadside. The man was wearing a very fashionable Western suit, and the woman looked like a well-educated woman. They were just arguing at first, but when they reached the climax, they started fighting; as a result, the woman could not beat the man, and the man just punched the woman one punch after another. At this time, among the people who gathered to watch the excitement, there was a vigorous young man who stood up, not only to rescue the woman, but also punched the man one punch after another. The person who was arguing with the woman earlier was obviously weaker and had to retreat to the foot of the wall, shouting:

"We are family, mind your own business!"

The vigorous young man answered cleverly: "Regardless of whether you are family or not, if you beat a woman outside, we will beat you; since you are family, why don't you go home to reason, why fight in the street?"

It was the woman who ran out to mediate, and the matter was concluded!

What is the meaning of this matter? Why do I want to bring it up? Nothing else, this also shows that there are still some people who understand respecting women.

"Respect women," some people must still oppose, they will say this: "Why respect women? Isn't it good for everyone to be equal? We don't want to oppress women like before!" However, these people have forgotten the characteristics of women: because they are physically and physically, after scholars have proven, they are far inferior to men; therefore, men, not only like Yi Fangshuo, had a wife and three concubines and wanted to marry a thirteen-year-old girl as the fourth concubine, we must strongly oppose, even letting a woman stand in a bumpy tram, and the man sits comfortably, we must also oppose! The former is to make the status of men and women equal, and the latter clearly contains the meaning of "respecting women"!

Although men should "respect women" everywhere, women should not think that they have gained the respect of men, and show arrogance and look down on everything!

Countryside and City 267

— Jue Fu

People who live in noisy and bustling big cities but cannot enjoy the blessings of urban civilization always yearn for a secluded and quiet rural life. In their minds, they often think: in spring, the fields are full of colorful flowers, and the streams and valleys are full of clear flowing water, lovely; in summer, everywhere is lush green jungle, chirping and singing cicadas, lovely; and in the late autumn with fallen leaves all over the ground, and the bleak winter with white snow all over the mountains and fields, the desolate and solemn scenery is also lovely. If it is a poet, as long as he walks there for a few days, he can bring back many soul-stirring poems, if it is an essayist, as long as he sits in the east wing and looks out at the fields on both sides, he can also write many fascinating sketches! (Many travel notes and sketches are written in this way).

However, is the countryside really as beautiful as people imagine in their minds and as depicted in the poet's pen? This may only be sitting in a sedan chair, listening to the creaking sound of the waterwheel, and busily chanting "the gentle breeze sends the sound of the waterwheel," such a touching line; like Lu Xun wrote in "Storm in a Teacup," sitting on a wine boat, looking out and seeing the villagers chatting while shaking large plantain fans, he immediately burst into poetic inspiration, saying: "Without thought and without worry, this is truly the joy of a farmer's family"! This kind of superficial observation! As for what Old Lady Nine Pounds said, they cannot hear it, and the situation that farmers are busy all year round and still cannot live a good life, they have not seen it—or are unwilling to see it.

"Revitalize the countryside," "Go to the countryside,"... these slogans were once shouted very loudly some time ago: but this is just everyone shouting when they are happy, and I have never seen anyone actually do it; even now, they feel tired and tasteless even shouting, and gradually become silent!—Perhaps the rise and fall of the countryside has little to do with these people who sleep in the city and praise the countryside!

Now, travel notes depicting the countryside as a paradise, and poems depicting the life of farmers as so leisurely and comfortable, can be seen everywhere again; this cannot help but admire the strong imagination of these artists!

Grandma Class Theory 268

— Jiang Sheng

Among women, the grandma class is the most useless. Living expenses are earned by the husband; brewing tea and cooking rice, sweeping the floor, wiping the table, washing clothes, and folding quilts, all have to be done by the old maids; buying boat tickets to cross the river, and buying tickets to go to the cinema, all have to be done by younger siblings.... In short, except for eating and playing mahjong, where one has to use both jade hands, the rest of the time, it is best to lie on a rocking chair and ask the maids to rub their legs for comfort.

The predecessors of grandmas, some are old-fashioned young ladies, some are new-style female students, and some are modern socialites. However, the old-fashioned young ladies can do needlework, the new-style female students can play table tennis and knit foreign rope clothes, and the modern socialites can shake hands, which can be said to be not entirely useless; only after becoming a grandma class, they are afraid of being shy when shaking hands, they are impatient to do needlework and knit clothes, and they have no strength to play table tennis. In a word, after a woman becomes a grandma, she simply becomes a useless waste.

Grandma Pitiful Theory

However, grandmas are also the most pitiful among women.

Young girls can jump around, and old women can laugh happily; but grandmas cannot.

The grandma class itself has no happiness, and takes the happiness of the husband class as its happiness. The husbands in the world cannot all have happiness: and some of the husband's happiness must be shared with parents, some must be shared with children, some must be shared with friends, and even some must be shared with enemies. Therefore, in terms of the entire grandma class, there is really no happiness at all.

When the old maid feels tired of working and is unhappy, she can immediately find a new one, and if the maid is wronged, she can also run away privately. However, the fate of the grandma class is doomed: a new environment is not easy to find, run away? Where is the courage? So the suffering of the grandma class must be endured for a lifetime.

Grandma Sinful Theory

In fact, the grandma class is a class that commits sins and does evil.

People belonging to the husband class, except for a very few, mostly have "serious business" to do in society: if society loses the activities of men, then this society will die immediately. However, the grandma class is unwilling to take into account this overall situation. They do not care about three or seven twenty-one, and always hope to hug their husbands in their arms and treat them as their hearts and livers, and they think they are happy. They only know how to enrich their own small world, and do not know that outside their small world, there is a big world.

Napoleon said: "Women are machines for bearing sons"! But many grandmas are too ignorant, and their environment does not allow them to raise sons, but she actually gives birth to sons, and even gives birth to as many as possible one after another. This will affect the husband's career and increase the burden of living. Many men in society commit crimes because they have to support their families. This account cannot but be placed on the grandma class.

However, if the grandma class does not give birth to sons at all, then the number will inevitably be extinct: so not giving birth to sons is also a sin.

Ghosts in the Swimming Pool 269

— Ge Ping

It is said that in the swimming pool of the Central Military Academy in Nanjing, "recently, there have been cries at night, and the water waves are also quite loud." It is said that "a student of the ninth term drowned in the swimming pool some time ago." So "whether the above news is caused by this," although "it is impossible to know"; but based on the fact that "when the weather was hot last time, students or service soldiers often sneaked to the pool to snore and cool off at night, but no one has gone recently," it is really a miracle of "something happened for a reason" and "found to have factual basis," "which is really worthy of scientists' research."

Although China is an advanced ancient civilization, science is not very prosperous. There are only a few scientists, and I am afraid they are busy with national affairs and have no time to study these boring questions of "not knowing life, how can we know death," or reluctantly study and still take out a sign of no ghosts to perfunctorily deal with it, and there is no magic weapon to suppress evil and search for ghosts to cure him; let the wronged ghost of a certain ninth-term student who drowned continue to act recklessly, making students unable to practice swimming in peace, and service soldiers dare not sneak to snore and cool off, what to do? Moreover, at the beginning of the month, our Miss China, the mermaid Ms. Yang, came back from Nanshi to show her skills, isn't she going to perform in Beijing? If the ghost dares to make waves, with Ms. Yang's bravery, it is of course not very important. But if it dares to "cry very sadly," then the tears of the hero may shatter the heart of the beauty.

Therefore, I dare to learn from Guangzhou comrade Liu Ridong's method of banning men and women from swimming and walking together, and offer a plan.

First, please invite Zhang Tianshi of the 63rd generation to Nanjing to set up an altar and conduct a ritual, and chase after and transcend a certain ninth-term student in the water, so that he can escape the ghost world, ascend to the immortal ranks forever, and bestow the title of Dragon King of the pool to guard the pool. Then not only will the pool no longer have drowning and haunting incidents, but also if there is a drought in the future, the residents of Nanjing can have an extra rain dragon king, and rain a few more inches of sweet rain.

Former Residence 270

— Bai She

The longing for my former residence has been in my heart every day for the past three years, but it's been limited to just longing. Two months ago, I traveled by boat from a water city in the South to Shanghai. On the morning of the fourth day, I entered the Wusong estuary. The desolation and chaos of Wusong were expected, but I climbed onto the rope ladder of the ship's mast, stretching my neck to look towards my former residence. Black smoke swirled in front of me. At that moment, a white wall and a small window seemed to emerge from behind the green trees, but when I tried to look more closely, I couldn't see anything at all. My former residence had been shelled, that was certainly true, but I couldn't believe that it would be as decayed as other buildings, like a pile of ruins, or even like a flattened wasteland.

Recently, I moved from Shanghai to a small street, and I felt a burst of joy and sorrow because this place is very close to my former residence. Every time I take a car to the train station, I have to pass near my former residence. Every time I pass, I always turn my head to look. Although my body is sitting in the car, my heart has long left. I hate why life is so hurried? I can't even take a look at my former residence when passing by.

But the opportunity finally came one day. On a sweltering afternoon, I hired a car to go near my former residence. Driven by some unknown psychology, I got out of the car before reaching my former residence, and identified the old-time roads among the weeds and rocks, quickly walking towards the familiar ground. The cobblestone road didn't seem to have the light of those days anymore, naturally due to the sparse number of pedestrians. The water in the small pond had dried up, and I didn't dare to expect to hear the noisy croaking of frogs here anymore. I turned a corner, and my feet told me that this was where my former residence was, but I still continued to walk forward. After walking a few steps, I turned back again, because looking ahead, it didn't look like my former residence at all.

Looking towards the west, the angle and distance between the short forest and my eyes proved that I was standing in front of the gate of my former residence. The footsteps of young men and women were no longer seen in front of the short forest. Looking back, who poured a bucket of cold water on my head? My God, there's no gate, no roof, no... just a vast expanse of emptiness. How can you ask me to believe it, how can you ask me to believe that this is my former residence?

A few pieces of broken bricks, is this the powdered wall where I hung my paintings? A few blades of grass, is this all of my property? Scorched earth, is this the trace of evening life? Is it? Is it? Yes! Mother, is it really true?

Is this where I painted wearing a black robe? Is this where I opened bottles of deep red wine with my friends? Yes, the green light on the table was like a lotus petal, so where is the green light? I never didn't know that everything in the world changes, that a paradise a hundred years ago can become a prison for confining prisoners, and that magnificent dance halls can be built under the barren land, but my former residence, you have changed too quickly, yes, my former residence was only recently built on barren land, and soon after was reduced to ashes again. My former residence, don't you think that your days of existence were too short, that you changed too quickly?

The sun is gradually setting in the west. Isn't this the time when I forgot everything under the window and devoted myself to painting? But I want to cry, I want to cry bitterly towards the setting sun, where is my former residence? Oh, my former residence!

To see my former residence again, unless it's in my memory.

Amateur Mailbox

Dependence on Others 271

— Editor

Dear Editor,

I am a young man without deep academic knowledge, but I did study in a private school for seven years when I was young. I also haven't learned any craftsmanship, and haven't even been an apprentice. Now I have something to ask for your careful guidance.

For me, without learning or knowledge, wanting to find a relatively good position in society is extremely difficult, to say the least. So for several years, I have been idle at home. Now it can be said that my luck has turned, and I have been introduced by a friend who works as a clerk in a certain company to be a clerk in his company. This is of course unexpectedly delightful, but with my abilities, how can I be competent? Therefore, I replied, "I'm afraid I don't have the ability!" He immediately replied, "It doesn't matter, I can help you with everything." So I became a clerk in this company, and it has been two months now. Speaking of it, I'm ashamed, but for the past two months, all the documents, except for a few simple ones, have been successfully completed with his help. But thinking carefully, relying on others for a long time, even though he is willing to help, if the director finds out after a long time, I will inevitably be expelled. Therefore, I want to study on my own in my spare time. According to colleagues, being a clerk here is not difficult, as long as one has a high school level, it is enough to cope with it. But with my level, how long will it take to reach the high school level at the fastest? What level is my current level equivalent to? Which self-study literature textbooks are the most complete? What is the proper procedure for self-study? The above questions are what I urgently need to know. Please give me an answer! If you have a better method than self-study, please give me careful guidance. I would be twelve times grateful to you. Best wishes

Sincerely, Liu Shao'an

Answer: Since you have such a good friend who is willing to sincerely and wholeheartedly promote you, the opportunity is extremely rare. Therefore, at this time, you should indeed work hard to study on your own and try to catch up. As long as a person has determination and perseverance, they can learn everything well. With your current level of education, it is of course immature, but you are definitely not without the qualifications to learn clerical work. You can practice and apply at the same time, and moreover, you have that good friend who can guide you from the side, so your learning will be more practical and your progress will be faster than the average person who studies official documents on their own. As for the high school level, it is originally a general statement. In reality, to do official documents, you only need to have fluent Chinese and be familiar with the format of official documents to start. The other subjects studied in high school are mostly not needed. Therefore, you should go directly to learning official documents now, and don't go around in circles to "study to the high school level." Practicing official documents cannot be effective by rote learning of model texts, nor can it be applied by rote memorizing some stock phrases. The main thing is to read more of the current incoming and outgoing documents, and at the same time, gather your courage and try it yourself. After you have done it yourself and feel that it is not appropriate, then you can refer to the model texts to see where your problems are. This way, progress will be very fast. The "Detailed Explanation of Current Official Document Formats" published by Huiwentang is a good book, and you can purchase it for reference.

Novel

Sundae Ice Cream 272

— Dai Ni

She jumped onto the weighing machine, and a beautiful face with big eyes was reflected in the glass mirror in front of her. She turned her head, and two surprised "Ah!" sounds came out.

"Long time no see."

"Yes. Buying a few things."

One in front, one behind, as if understanding each other, they walked towards the cosmetics department.

The female staff member greeted them with a beaming smile. She bent over to choose the fragrance she needed from the glass cabinet. The other stood behind, showing his head, like a newly married couple.

"This." She stretched out her slender index finger and pointed to a delicate powder box in the glass cabinet.

"This is Feisibeizhi." He brought his head a little closer.

The female staff member hurriedly handed it out and said, "This brand has only been in Shanghai for less than two months, and the price is also cheap;" she turned over the bottom of the box, "four yuan, nine jiao, and a half."

"Okay, take two boxes," she quickly pulled out a ten-yuan bill from her handbag.

The other took out a handkerchief from his trouser pocket and covered his nose.

From the cosmetics to the handkerchief department, one in front, one behind.

Like this, like that, she chose several kinds of colored handkerchiefs, and finally picked out the largest silk one and said to him, "Do you want to buy one too?"

The other nodded, and the money was handed to the female staff member from the handbag.

Slowly walking forward from the handkerchief department, he asked;

"Is there anything else you want to buy?"

"Let's have some ice cream."

They went through the side door to the ice cream parlor and sat down facing each other.

"Two sundaes." She instructed the waiter.

Colored ice cream was placed in front of them, and she skillfully scooped it up with a white copper spoon.

"It's really hot!"

"But my heart is cold!" She stared at the other person.

"Do you still hate me?" He moved his head a little closer.

"It's really hot." He pretended not to hear, and took out a new handkerchief to cover his nose.

After a while, without a word, the ice cream turned into water in the white porcelain basin.

"Mei," she stared at the other person for a long time, "are you married?"

"A woman who loved me ran away!"

"How venomous! There's no way!"

"So I'm not getting married again." He raised his head and called the waiter. She reached out and handed over a bill.

"Sorry for the trouble." He lit a cigarette.

"Always like that!" she said resentfully.

"Is there anything else?" he smiled.

"Let's go home."

They stood up at the same time, and she walked towards the side door.

"Isn't it the same to go this way?" He pointed to the main door of the ice cream parlor.

"My car is waiting over there," she replied.

"Oh... oh... then goodbye." (End)

Shen Bao Local Supplement, Film Special

A Three-Sided View on the "Film Vernacular" Debate 273

— Mo Shuai

Whether it is a product of the "Literary vs. Vernacular War," or a discovery by a small group of "specialists," the construction of a "vernacular" language for the masses—a language that the masses can speak, understand, write, and read; the definite need for a "unified language"—is at least worthy of our clarion call.

In fact, what do we see? Above the black characters on white paper, we are given some abstract arguments; don't say that this is a "habitual skill" of the Chinese people.

Recently, we have read enough of the review articles on "vernacular" and film in this publication. In his article "Vernacular and Film Themes," Mr. Bingyang said: If the theme we adopt is centered on a certain rural village in Jiangnan, then we cannot completely use "Mandarin" here. Here, we have to quote some dialects and local languages... But Mr. Danfeng's article "The Application of Vernacular in Films" means: Vernacular is neither "classical Chinese" nor "vernacular," nor "dialects" or "local languages," but is constructed in another way. However, it only gives an example of saying, "If it doesn't rain, what should we do?"

Mr. Tang Na, because Mr. Danfeng wrote the sentence "At present, we strongly oppose the filming of Cantonese dialogue sound films" in his article, also came up with a large-scale denunciation. The reason is that Mr. Tang Na published an article "Cantonese Sound Films and Vernacular Construction" in Daily Film, and he agreed with filmmakers to film Cantonese films; however, many places also said one-sided words. For example: "According to Mr. Danfeng's statement, advocating Mandarin on the screen now can help eliminate classical Chinese, but as a result, Cantonese audiences don't understand Mandarin, and I'm afraid it will be as alienated and difficult to understand as watching British and American sound films without understanding English." Then, according to Mr. Tang Na's statement, if Cantonese sound films are shown to audiences who do not understand Cantonese, will it not be as alienating and difficult to understand as watching British and American sound films without understanding English? As a matter of fact, in the current China, Mandarin, which is considered official language style, is at least more widespread than Cantonese dialect.

The construction of the vernacular in film has formed the following three theories: (1) Mr. Bingyang's theory is to form a "vernacular" by mixing "dialects" and "local languages" into "Mandarin," which is an impossible thing: in fact, in our special China, each province has its own "dialects" and "local languages," and each village has its own "dialects" and "local languages." Even the language of the south gate - north gate east gate - west gate of each city can find many, many absolutely different words. Due to the inconsistency of "dialects" and "local languages," of course, the language of place A will be completely incomprehensible to people in place B; if our film theme is centered on a certain rural village and mixes in the "dialects" and "local languages" of that place, the films to be shot in the future can only be limited to being shown in a certain rural village, unless they are translated into the "dialects" and "local languages" of other rural villages in another screening location.

(2) Mr. Danfeng's is not "classical Chinese," "vernacular," "dialects," or "local languages," but needs to build another simple and easy-to-understand sentence in the so-called "vernacular" used in film, but before we start building anything, we can temporarily not talk about it.

(3) Mr. Tang Na advocates the highly developed dissolution of "dialects" to make it a naturalized vernacular (see Mr. Tang Na's original work on the 23rd and 24th of this publication), but in fact it will not be as easy and simple as Mr. Tang Na's ideal. For example, take "Cantonese sound films" as an example. First, can this "Cantonese sound film" allow the masses who are not Cantonese to appreciate it? Second, if they occasionally watch it, can they thoroughly understand it? Third, even if they can understand it partially, can it cause a dissolving effect between the Cantonese language and their own language? This is a very important thing to pay attention to. Moreover, we cannot just take one or two "dialects" to highly dissolve it and think it is "vernacular." We should dissolve the "dialects" of the whole country to be in line with what Mr. Tang Na said is a naturally growing "unified Mandarin"; then, the dozens of dialects in China on a small scale, and the hundreds of dialects on an expanded scale, need to be highly developed at the same time, and I'm afraid all the film companies in China will not be able to afford it? If there is a Cantonese film for a while, and a Jiangxi film for a while, it will be even more of a mess, and it will be difficult to advance or retreat.

Finally, I have to say: At this time, we can completely abandon the beautiful name of "vernacular." We should do the work of unifying the language, and I advocate less "empty talk" and more "hard work." We hope that everyone will implement everyone's claims. After several years, whoever's claim is to achieve the success of unifying the language one day is also the day when the "vernacular" is born; it is also the day when whoever's claim to create the "vernacular" reaches the "victory" goal.

In Memory of Marie Dressler 274

— Huang Yingdai

According to news from Santa Barbara, the old star Marie Dressler finally passed away on the 28th after a period of suffering, at the age of 61. Marie Dressler suffered from very complex illnesses this time, including heart disease and kidney disease. She had died twice during her illness, but both times she was resuscitated. It wasn't until this time that she couldn't struggle for life anymore. She was born in Canada on November 9, 1873, and devoted herself to the stage in 1886, meeting the audience for the first time. She was only thirteen years old at the time. She was dedicated to her profession and was willing to study it until 1914, when she joined the film industry. Later, she once left the film industry and returned to the stage. *Tillie's Punctured Romance* was a comedy and the first film she shot. Following that, *Tugboat Annie* was considered the most successful work. Among the films she starred in, she worked very enthusiastically and was willing to help with anything that was needed of her. Many of the films she starred in have been successful, and she is now the most beloved star in Hollywood. Millions of moviegoers will feel very sorry to hear the news of her death. The death of this big star will cause some major losses to Hollywood, right?

Marie Dressler is dead, but the impression she left on this world will never be erased. We believe that at least in this twentieth century, the people will not forget the deep impression she gave. Her private life is the same as on the screen, full of happy colors. From the age of thirteen, when she joined the Benotto Meldon Troupe to perform drama, to the end of the nineteenth century, until recently, with the film *Her Sweetheart*, her impression has long been deeply rooted in the hearts of people all over the world. Her film life began when Mack Sennett signed a contract with her at the height of his fame, and she became famous after starring in *Tillie's Punctured Romance*. Following that, her famous films *Anna Christie*, *Emma*, *Min* and *Bill Tugboat Annie* were quite successful, and perhaps the most successful work was the recent *Dinner At Eight*. She had many close friends, and many of them were celebrities. She treated her friends as sincerely and genuinely as she did on the screen. She also liked to support charitable causes throughout her life. Tens of millions of movie fans in this world will regret hearing about the death of Marie Dressler, and thousands of people who knew her will mourn for her!

*Willow Dark, Flowers Bright*, starring the new star Constance Cummings, is a story that combines sorrow and joy, and the performance is very moving. It will be released at the Cathay soon.

Li Lin Haiwei's Life 275

— Hai Qing

The great, hard-working Li Lin Haiwei is successful. Her numerous films have made a deep impression. Her singing voice and dancing style have intoxicated many people! Looking at her petite figure, one always thinks she is a sickly Lin Daiyu, but no, she is a big star in the sports world! She can play ball, swim, tightrope walk, and ice skate. What is most rare is that she can ride unruly horses. She has an indomitable will and a spirit of advancement; all of this has contributed to her current reputation. She is always very busy every day, and she can't stay still even at home, especially when reporters come to inquire and take pictures of her.

Li Lin Haiwei's style, her bird-like demeanor, and her childish temper can be seen in almost every film. Moreover, because of her gifted singing voice, there will always be a song in her films. Films such as *Dragon Soaring Phoenix Dancing*, *Peach Blossom Village*, and *Phoenix Seeking Phoenix* can all fit her personality and fully develop her performance. She is very suitable for those lighthearted works with songs and dances, and each performance will not disappoint.

She was born in London and is already twenty-seven years old this year. She is originally German, but her mother is British. In addition to English and German, she can also speak French. Therefore, her films are sometimes in English, sometimes in German, and sometimes in French, but they are all equally fluent and delightful.

Their Swimming Companions 276

Li Zhuozhuo came to Shanghai from Hong Kong. Originally, she was going to play the lead actress in the "Whirlpool" directed by Yang Xiaozhong of Lianhua Third Factory, but Li had to return to Hong Kong because she had a play to shoot in Hong Kong, so the role of "Whirlpool" was chosen by someone else. Li Zhuozhuo is good at swimming. Her swimming skills were once shown in "Breaking Waves," but according to people, she didn't fully develop her skills there. This time she came to Shanghai, in those days when the thermometer was over 100 degrees, she ran to the Lanyuan Swimming Pool every morning. Her various swimming skill performances were indeed much higher. Therefore, her colleagues at Lianhua called her Mermaid II, especially Lin Chuchu, Chen Yanyan, Li Keng, etc., because they saw her swimming skills and were very envious. So when they went swimming together, they asked Zhuozhuo to make several poses for them to watch. Zhuozhuo is very humorous, and sometimes she even pretends to be a teacher, for example, if Li Keng doesn't swim well, she picks him up and spanks his bottom. Now that Zhuozhuo has returned to Hong Kong, Chuchu, Yanyan, and Li Keng have lost a swimming companion.

Film Novel

A Good Son, A Good Wife (Born to be Kissed) (Part 2) 277

— Written by: Xin Zhi

Yi Di's eyes searched all around for Ke Xin Si, but she could not see him. She knew that Ke Xin Si must be talking with that Mr. Pan Qi. Ke Xin Si was indeed talking with Pan Qi, but after speaking three or five sentences, he already knew that the conversation was superfluous. He had already decided on his next move. Pan Qi was the only person who could save him, but searching through Pan Qi's past history, there was no discovery of him having any compassion for a bleeding and dying enemy. Pan Qi had struggled out of poverty to rise to the ranks of the gentry. He had tasted the bitterness of hunger, cold, and disappointment. He had also experienced failure and tragedy. Finally, he had also tasted the taste of victory. He had money, and he also had power. Friends also gathered around him. Opportunities were also easily available. As for the splendor of the palace and the luxury of daily life, these were especially minor matters. But after all of this, he had not learned the meaning of the two words "benevolence and love." "Listen, Pan Qi," Ke Xin Si made this last request, "If you would strike me less... give me some breathing room... the situation won't get so bad... I still have quite a bit of property." Pan Qi said inhumanely, "You don't have a single penny, haven't you already owed twenty different ways. But you don't need to worry so much, there are quite a few who sympathize with you... and they are not all as rude as me, there are many prominent families among them." Ke Xin Si listened and remained silent. Pan Qi smirked, stood up, left Ke Xin Si's elegantly decorated study, and walked into the large living room.

Before her second performance, Yi Di quickly changed her clothes, and feeling that she had some free time, she slipped out of the large crowd and secretly opened the door to Ke Xin Si's study and went inside. Ke Xin Si was sitting at his desk. When he saw an uninvited guest suddenly appear, he quickly pushed the open drawer closed. Unconsciously, he rubbed his hands together, as if he had just put down something cold and wanted to warm his hands. He was absent-minded and looked at Yi Di without seeing her. Yi Di smiled charmingly and said, "I'm afraid I've disturbed you." His gaze seemed clearer, and he looked at her strangely and said, "It's okay." Yi Di sat down impolitely on the corner of his desk. She coquettishly said, "You must be the happiest person in the world." Ke Xin Si smiled bitterly and said, "What makes you think that?" Yi Di smiled and said, "Because you already have everything in the world. Look, what a beautiful home... and..." she self-importantly speculated, "you're already engaged and will be getting married soon." Ke Xin Si seemed to admire her cleverness and smiled again, saying, "I am neither engaged nor married." Yi Di leaned forward and asked, "Then, how are you able to stand it?" Ke Xin Si frowned and pretended to think, saying, "Perhaps it's because I've never met you before." He took out cigarettes and offered one to the guest, but Yi Di politely declined. He said, "Oh, you don't even have this little sin?" Yi Di said, "People always say how romantic and flirtatious the singers are. But as for me, Mr. Ke Xin Si, I've been on Broadway for so long, but I'm still the same as when I left home." She patted Ke Xin Si's hand. He felt that Ke Xin Si didn't quite believe her words, so she silently sat down and picked up a small bronze figure from the table and played with it. She said, "I am also a person who is fascinated by art." (To be continued)
